<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acid-base_properties">Acid-base properties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Acid-base properties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As an acid, sulfuric acid reacts with most <a href="/wiki/Base_(chemistry)" title="Base (chemistry)">bases</a> to give the corresponding sulfate. For example, the blue <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a> salt <a href="/wiki/Copper(II)_sulfate" title="Copper(II) sulfate">copper(II) sulfate</a>, commonly used for <a href="/wiki/Electroplating" title="Electroplating">electroplating</a> and as a <a href="/wiki/Fungicide" title="Fungicide">fungicide</a>, is prepared by the reaction of <a href="/wiki/Copper(II)_oxide" title="Copper(II) oxide">copper(II) oxide</a> with sulfuric acid:
</p>
<dl><dd>CuO (s) + <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> (aq) → <span class="chemf nowrap">CuSO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> (aq) + <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> (l)</dd></dl>
<p>Sulfuric acid can also be used to displace weaker acids from their salts. Reaction with <a href="/wiki/Sodium_acetate" title="Sodium acetate">sodium acetate</a>, for example, displaces <a href="/wiki/Acetic_acid" title="Acetic acid">acetic acid</a>, <span class="chemf nowrap">CH<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span>COOH</span>, and forms <a href="/wiki/Sodium_bisulfate" title="Sodium bisulfate">sodium bisulfate</a>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> + <span class="chemf nowrap">CH<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span>COONa</span> → <span class="chemf nowrap">NaHSO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> + <span class="chemf nowrap">CH<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span>COOH</span></dd></dl>
<p>Similarly, reacting sulfuric acid with <a href="/wiki/Potassium_nitrate" title="Potassium nitrate">potassium nitrate</a> can be used to produce <a href="/wiki/Nitric_acid" title="Nitric acid">nitric acid</a> and a precipitate of <a href="/wiki/Potassium_bisulfate" title="Potassium bisulfate">potassium bisulfate</a>. When combined with <a href="/wiki/Nitric_acid" title="Nitric acid">nitric acid</a>, sulfuric acid acts both as an acid and a dehydrating agent, forming the <a href="/wiki/Nitronium_ion" title="Nitronium ion">nitronium ion</a> <span class="chemf nowrap">NO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span>, which is important in <a href="/wiki/Nitration" title="Nitration">nitration</a> reactions involving <a href="/wiki/Electrophilic_aromatic_substitution" title="Electrophilic aromatic substitution">electrophilic aromatic substitution</a>. This type of reaction, where protonation occurs on an <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> atom, is important in many <a href="/wiki/Organic_chemistry" title="Organic chemistry">organic chemistry</a> reactions, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fischer_esterification" title="Fischer esterification">Fischer esterification</a> and dehydration of alcohols.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Structure_of_protonated_sulfuric_acid.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="953" data-file-width="1308" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Structure_of_protonated_sulfuric_acid.png/200px-Structure_of_protonated_sulfuric_acid.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Structure_of_protonated_sulfuric_acid.png/300px-Structure_of_protonated_sulfuric_acid.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Structure_of_protonated_sulfuric_acid.png/400px-Structure_of_protonated_sulfuric_acid.png 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Structure_of_protonated_sulfuric_acid.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Solid state structure of the [D<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>4</sub>]<sup>+</sup> ion present in [D<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>4</sub>]<sup>+</sup>[SbF<sub>6</sub>]<sup>−</sup>, synthesized by using <a href="/wiki/Deuterium" title="Deuterium">D</a>F in place of HF. (see text)</div></div></div>
<p>When allowed to react with <a href="/wiki/Superacid" title="Superacid">superacids</a>, sulfuric acid can act as a base and be protonated, forming the [H<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>4</sub>]<sup>+</sup> ion. Salt of [H<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>4</sub>]<sup>+</sup> have been prepared using the following reaction in liquid <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_fluoride" title="Hydrogen fluoride">HF</a>:
</p>
<dl><dd>((CH<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>SiO)<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>2</sub> + 3 HF + SbF<sub>5</sub> → [H<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>4</sub>]<sup>+</sup>[SbF<sub>6</sub>]<sup>−</sup> + 2 (CH<sub>3</sub>)<sub>3</sub>SiF</dd></dl>
<p>The above reaction is thermodynamically favored due to the high <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bond_enthalpy" title="Bond enthalpy">bond enthalpy</a> of the Si–F bond in the side product. Protonation using simply <a href="/wiki/Fluoroantimonic_acid" title="Fluoroantimonic acid">HF/SbF<sub>5</sub></a>, however, have met with failure, as pure sulfuric acid undergoes <a href="/wiki/Molecular_autoionization" title="Molecular autoionization">self-ionization</a> to give [H<sub>3</sub>O]<sup>+</sup> ions, which prevents the conversion of H<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> to [H<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>4</sub>]<sup>+</sup> by the HF/SbF<sub>5</sub> system:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InorgChem_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-InorgChem-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd>2 H<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> ⇌ [H<sub>3</sub>O]<sup>+</sup> + [HS<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>]<sup>−</sup></dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions_with_metals_and_strong_oxidizing_property">Reactions with metals and strong oxidizing property</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Reactions with metals and strong oxidizing property">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Dilute sulfuric acid reacts with metals via a single displacement reaction as with other typical <a href="/wiki/Acid" title="Acid">acids</a>, producing <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a> gas and <a href="/wiki/Salt_(chemistry)" title="Salt (chemistry)">salts</a> (the metal sulfate). It attacks reactive metals (metals at positions above <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Reactivity_series" title="Reactivity series">reactivity series</a>) such as <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">iron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aluminium" title="Aluminium">aluminium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magnesium" title="Magnesium">magnesium</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nickel" title="Nickel">nickel</a>.
</p>
<dl><dd>Fe (s) + <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> (aq) → <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> (g) + <span class="chemf nowrap">FeSO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> (aq)</dd></dl>
<p>However, concentrated sulfuric acid is a <a href="/wiki/Oxidizing_agent" title="Oxidizing agent">strong oxidizing agent</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OA_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-OA-5">[5]</a></sup> and does not react with metals in the same way as other typical <a href="/wiki/Acid" title="Acid">acids</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">Sulfur dioxide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">water</a> and <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2−</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> ions are evolved instead of the <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salt_(chemistry)" title="Salt (chemistry)">salts</a>.
</p>
<dl><dd>2 H<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> + 2 e<sup>−</sup> → SO<sub>2</sub> + 2 H<sub>2</sub>O + <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2−</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span></dd></dl>
<p>It can oxidize non-active metals such as <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>, depending upon the temperature.
</p>
<dl><dd>Cu + 2 H<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> → SO<sub>2</sub> + 2 H<sub>2</sub>O + <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2−</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> + Cu<sup>2+</sup></dd></dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lead" title="Lead">Lead</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tungsten" title="Tungsten">tungsten</a>, however, are resistant to sulfuric acid.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions_with_non-metals">Reactions with non-metals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Reactions with non-metals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hot concentrated sulfuric acid oxidizes non-metals such as <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">carbon</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> (as bituminous coal) and <a href="/wiki/Sulfur" title="Sulfur">sulfur</a>.
</p>
<dl><dd>C + 2 H<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> → CO<sub>2</sub> + 2 SO<sub>2</sub> + 2 H<sub>2</sub>O</dd>
<dd>S + 2 H<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> → 3 SO<sub>2</sub> + 2 H<sub>2</sub>O</dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reaction_with_sodium_chloride">Reaction with sodium chloride</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Reaction with sodium chloride">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It reacts with <a href="/wiki/Sodium_chloride" title="Sodium chloride">sodium chloride</a>, and gives <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_chloride" title="Hydrogen chloride">hydrogen chloride</a> <a href="/wiki/Gas" title="Gas">gas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sodium_bisulfate" title="Sodium bisulfate">sodium bisulfate</a>:
</p>
<dl><dd>NaCl + H<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> → NaHSO<sub>4</sub> + HCl</dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electrophilic_aromatic_substitution">Electrophilic aromatic substitution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Electrophilic aromatic substitution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Benzene undergoes <a href="/wiki/Electrophilic_aromatic_substitution" title="Electrophilic aromatic substitution">electrophilic aromatic substitution</a> with sulfuric acid to give the corresponding <a href="/wiki/Sulfonic_acid" title="Sulfonic acid">sulfonic acids</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BenzeneSulfonation.png"><img alt="BenzeneSulfonation.png" data-file-height="514" data-file-width="1740" height="74" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/BenzeneSulfonation.png/250px-BenzeneSulfonation.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/BenzeneSulfonation.png/375px-BenzeneSulfonation.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/BenzeneSulfonation.png/500px-BenzeneSulfonation.png 2x" width="250"/></a></dd></dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Occurrence">Occurrence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Occurrence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="488" data-file-width="650" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg/250px-Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg/375px-Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg/500px-Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rio_tinto_river_CarolStoker_NASA_Ames_Research_Center.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rio_Tinto_(river)" title="Rio Tinto (river)">Rio Tinto</a> with its highly acidic water</div></div></div>
<p>Pure sulfuric acid is not encountered naturally on Earth in anhydrous form, due to its great <a href="/wiki/Hygroscopy" title="Hygroscopy">affinity for water</a>. Dilute sulfuric acid is a constituent of <a href="/wiki/Acid_rain" title="Acid rain">acid rain</a>, which is formed by atmospheric <a href="/wiki/Redox" title="Redox">oxidation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a> in the presence of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_(molecule)" title="Water (molecule)">water</a> – i.e., oxidation of <a href="/wiki/Sulfurous_acid" title="Sulfurous acid">sulfurous acid</a>. Sulfur dioxide is the main byproduct produced when sulfur-containing fuels such as coal or oil are burned.
</p><p>Sulfuric acid is formed naturally by the oxidation of sulfide minerals, such as iron sulfide. The resulting water can be highly acidic and is called <a href="/wiki/Acid_mine_drainage" title="Acid mine drainage">acid mine drainage</a> (AMD) or acid rock drainage (ARD). This acidic water is capable of dissolving metals present in sulfide ores, which results in brightly colored, toxic streams. The oxidation of <a href="/wiki/Pyrite" title="Pyrite">pyrite</a> (iron sulfide) by molecular oxygen produces iron(II), or <span class="chemf nowrap">Fe<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span>:
</p>
<dl><dd>2 <span class="chemf nowrap">FeS<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> (s) + 7 <span class="chemf nowrap">O<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> + 2 <span class="Unicode"> </span><a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">H<sub>2</sub>O</a> → 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">Fe<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> + 4 <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2−</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> + 4 <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span></dd></dl>
<p>The <span class="chemf nowrap">Fe<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> can be further oxidized to <span class="chemf nowrap">Fe<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span>:
</p>
<dl><dd>4 <span class="chemf nowrap">Fe<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> + <span class="chemf nowrap">O<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> + 4 <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> → 4 <span class="chemf nowrap">Fe<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> + 2 <span class="Unicode"> </span><a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">H<sub>2</sub>O</a></dd></dl>
<p>The <span class="chemf nowrap">Fe<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> produced can be precipitated as the <a href="/wiki/Hydroxide" title="Hydroxide">hydroxide</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydrous_iron_oxides" title="Hydrous iron oxides">hydrous oxide</a>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="chemf nowrap">Fe<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> + 3 <span class="Unicode"> </span><a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">H<sub>2</sub>O</a> → <span class="chemf nowrap">Fe(OH)<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span>↓ + 3 <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span></dd></dl>
<p>The iron(III) ion ("ferric iron") can also oxidize pyrite:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="chemf nowrap">FeS<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span>(s) + 14 <span class="chemf nowrap">Fe<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> + 8 <span class="Unicode"> </span><a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">H<sub>2</sub>O</a> → 15 <span class="chemf nowrap">Fe<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span> + 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2−</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> + 16 <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">+</sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sub></span></span></dd></dl>
<p>When iron(III) oxidation of pyrite occurs, the process can become rapid. <a href="/wiki/PH" title="PH">pH</a> values below zero have been measured in ARD produced by this process.
</p><p>ARD can also produce sulfuric acid at a slower rate, so that the <a href="/wiki/Acid_neutralizing_capacity" title="Acid neutralizing capacity">acid neutralizing capacity</a> (ANC) of the aquifer can neutralize the produced acid. In such cases, the <a href="/wiki/Total_dissolved_solids" title="Total dissolved solids">total dissolved solids</a> (TDS) concentration of the water can be increased from the dissolution of minerals from the acid-neutralization reaction with the minerals.
</p><p>Sulfuric acid is used as a defense by certain marine species, for example, the phaeophyte alga <i>Desmarestia munda</i> (order <a href="/wiki/Desmarestiales" title="Desmarestiales">Desmarestiales</a>) concentrates sulfuric acid in cell vacuoles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pelletreau_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pelletreau-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stratospheric_aerosol">Stratospheric aerosol</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Stratospheric aerosol">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Stratosphere" title="Stratosphere">stratosphere</a>, the atmosphere's second layer that is generally between 10 and 50 km above Earth's surface, sulfuric acid is formed by the oxidation of volcanic sulfur dioxide by the <a href="/wiki/Hydroxyl_radical" title="Hydroxyl radical">hydroxyl radical</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kremser_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kremser-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> + HO<sup>•</sup> → <span class="chemf nowrap">HSO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span></dd>
<dd><span class="chemf nowrap">HSO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> + <span class="chemf nowrap">O<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> → <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> + <span class="chemf nowrap">HO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span></dd>
<dd><span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> + <span class="Unicode"> </span><a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">H<sub>2</sub>O</a> → <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span></dd></dl>
<p>Because sulfuric acid reaches <a href="/wiki/Supersaturation" title="Supersaturation">supersaturation</a> in the stratosphere, it can nucleate aerosol particles and provide a surface for aerosol growth via condensation and coagulation with other water-sulfuric acid aerosols. This results in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stratospheric_aerosol_layer" title="Stratospheric aerosol layer">stratospheric aerosol layer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kremser_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kremser-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extraterrestrial_sulfuric_acid">Extraterrestrial sulfuric acid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Extraterrestrial sulfuric acid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Venus">Venus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Venus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Sulfuric acid is produced in the upper atmosphere of <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Photochemistry" title="Photochemistry">photochemical</a> action on <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Water" title="Water">water</a> vapor. <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet">Ultraviolet</a> <a href="/wiki/Photon" title="Photon">photons</a> of wavelengths less than 169 <a href="/wiki/Nanometre" title="Nanometre">nm</a> can <a href="/wiki/Photodissociation" title="Photodissociation">photodissociate</a> carbon dioxide into <a href="/wiki/Carbon_monoxide" title="Carbon monoxide">carbon monoxide</a> and atomic <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a>. Atomic oxygen is highly reactive. When it reacts with sulfur dioxide, a trace component of the Venusian atmosphere, the result is <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_trioxide" title="Sulfur trioxide">sulfur trioxide</a>, which can combine with water vapor, another trace component of Venus's atmosphere, to yield sulfuric acid. In the upper, cooler portions of Venus's atmosphere, sulfuric acid exists as a liquid, and thick sulfuric acid clouds completely obscure the planet's surface when viewed from above. The main cloud layer extends from 45–70 km above the planet's surface, with thinner hazes extending as low as 30 km and as high as 90 km above the surface. The permanent Venusian clouds produce a concentrated acid rain, as the clouds in the atmosphere of Earth produce water rain.
</p><p>The atmosphere exhibits a sulfuric acid cycle. As sulfuric acid rain droplets fall down through the hotter layers of the atmosphere's temperature gradient, they are heated up and release water vapor, becoming more and more concentrated. When they reach temperatures above 300 °C, sulfuric acid begins to decompose into <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_trioxide" title="Sulfur trioxide">sulfur trioxide</a> and water, both in the gas phase. Sulfur trioxide is highly reactive and dissociates into sulfur dioxide and atomic oxygen, which oxidizes traces of carbon monoxide to form carbon dioxide. Sulfur dioxide and water vapor rise on convection currents from the mid-level atmospheric layers to higher altitudes, where they will be transformed again into sulfuric acid, and the cycle repeats.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Europa">Europa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Europa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Infrared spectra taken by <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Galileo_(spacecraft)" title="Galileo (spacecraft)"><i>Galileo</i> spacecraft</a> show distinct absorptions on <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a>'s moon <a href="/wiki/Europa_(moon)" title="Europa (moon)">Europa</a> that have been attributed to one or more sulfuric acid hydrates. Sulfuric acid in solution with water causes significant <a href="/wiki/Freezing-point_depression" title="Freezing-point depression">freezing-point depression</a> of water's <a href="/wiki/Melting_point" title="Melting point">melting point</a>, down to 210 K (−63 °C), and this would make the existence of liquid solutions beneath <a href="/wiki/Europa_(moon)" title="Europa (moon)">Europa</a>'s icy crust more likely. The interpretation of the spectra is somewhat controversial. Some planetary scientists prefer to assign the spectral features to the sulfate ion, perhaps as part of one or more minerals on Europa's surface.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Manufacture">Manufacture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Manufacture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Contact_process" title="Contact process">Contact process</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wet_sulfuric_acid_process" title="Wet sulfuric acid process">Wet sulfuric acid process</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lead_chamber_process" title="Lead chamber process">Lead chamber process</a></div>
<p>Sulfuric acid is produced from <a href="/wiki/Sulfur" title="Sulfur">sulfur</a>, oxygen and water via the conventional <a href="/wiki/Contact_process" title="Contact process">contact process</a> (DCDA) or the <a href="/wiki/Wet_sulfuric_acid_process" title="Wet sulfuric acid process">wet sulfuric acid process</a> (WSA).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contact_process">Contact process</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Contact process">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Contact_process" title="Contact process">Contact process</a></div>
<p>In the first step, sulfur is burned to produce sulfur dioxide.
</p>
<dl><dd>S (s) + <span class="chemf nowrap">O<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> (g) → <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> (g)</dd></dl>
<p>This is then oxidized to sulfur trioxide using oxygen in the presence of a <a href="/wiki/Vanadium(V)_oxide" title="Vanadium(V) oxide">vanadium(V) oxide</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catalyst" title="Catalyst">catalyst</a>. This reaction is reversible and the formation of the sulfur trioxide is exothermic.
</p>
<dl><dd>2 <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> (g) + <span class="chemf nowrap">O<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> (g) ⇌ 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> (g) (in presence of <span class="chemf nowrap">V<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">5</sub></span></span>)</dd></dl>
<p>The sulfur trioxide is absorbed into 97–98% <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> to form <a href="/wiki/Oleum" title="Oleum">oleum</a> (<span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>S<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">7</sub></span></span>), also known as fuming sulfuric acid. The oleum is then diluted with water to form concentrated sulfuric acid.
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> (l) + <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> (g)→ <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>S<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">7</sub></span></span> (l)</dd>
<dd><span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>S<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">7</sub></span></span> (l) + <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> (l) → 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> (l)</dd></dl>
<p>Directly dissolving <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> in water is not practical due to the highly <a href="/wiki/Exothermic_reaction" title="Exothermic reaction">exothermic</a> nature of the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_reaction" title="Chemical reaction">reaction</a> between sulfur trioxide and water. The reaction forms a corrosive aerosol that is very difficult to separate, instead of a liquid.
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> (g) + <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> (l) → <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span> (l)</dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wet_sulfuric_acid_process">Wet sulfuric acid process</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Wet sulfuric acid process">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wet_sulfuric_acid_process" title="Wet sulfuric acid process">Wet sulfuric acid process</a></div>
<p>In the first step, sulfur is burned to produce sulfur dioxide:
</p>
<dl><dd>S(s) + <span class="chemf nowrap">O<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span>(g) → <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span>(g)</dd></dl>
<p>or, alternatively, <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_sulfide" title="Hydrogen sulfide">hydrogen sulfide</a> (<span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>S</span>) gas is incinerated to <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> gas:
</p>
<dl><dd>2 <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>S</span> + 3 <span class="chemf nowrap">O<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> → 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> + 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> (−518 kJ/mol)</dd></dl>
<p>This is then oxidized to sulfur trioxide using oxygen with <a href="/wiki/Vanadium(V)_oxide" title="Vanadium(V) oxide">vanadium(V) oxide</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catalyst" title="Catalyst">catalyst</a>.
</p>
<dl><dd>2 <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> + <span class="chemf nowrap">O<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> → 2 <span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> (−99 kJ/mol) (reaction is reversible)</dd></dl>
<p>The sulfur trioxide is hydrated into sulfuric acid <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="chemf nowrap">SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">3</sub></span></span> + <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>O</span> → <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span>(g) (−101 kJ/mol)</dd></dl>
<p>The last step is the condensation of the sulfuric acid to liquid 97–98% <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span>(g) → <span class="chemf nowrap">H<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span>SO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">4</sub></span></span>(l) (−69 kJ/mol)</dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_methods">Other methods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Other methods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Another method is the less well-known metabisulfite method, in which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metabisulfite" title="Metabisulfite">metabisulfite</a> is placed at the bottom of a beaker, and 12.6 molar concentration <a href="/wiki/Hydrochloric_acid" title="Hydrochloric acid">hydrochloric acid</a> is added. The resulting gas is bubbled through <a href="/wiki/Nitric_acid" title="Nitric acid">nitric acid</a>, which will release brown/red vapors. The completion of the reaction is indicated by the ceasing of the fumes. This method does not produce an inseparable mist, which is quite convenient.
</p>
<dl><dd>SO<sub>2</sub> + HNO<sub>3</sub> + H<sub>2</sub>O→ H<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> + NO</dd></dl>
<p>Sulfuric acid can be produced in the laboratory by burning sulfur in air and dissolving the gas produced in a <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_peroxide" title="Hydrogen peroxide">hydrogen peroxide</a> solution.
</p>
<dl><dd>SO<sub>2</sub> + H<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> → H<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub></dd></dl>
<p>Prior to 1900, most sulfuric acid was manufactured by the <a href="/wiki/Lead_chamber_process" title="Lead chamber process">lead chamber process</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> As late as 1940, up to 50% of sulfuric acid manufactured in the United States was produced by chamber process plants.
</p><p>In early to mid nineteenth century "vitriol" plants existed, among other places, in <a href="/wiki/Prestonpans" title="Prestonpans">Prestonpans</a> in Scotland, <a href="/wiki/Shropshire" title="Shropshire">Shropshire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lagan_Valley" title="Lagan Valley">Lagan Valley</a> in County Antrim Ireland where it was used as a bleach for linen. Early bleaching of linen was done using lactic acid from sour milk but this was a slow process and the use of vitriol sped up the bleaching process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Uses">Uses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Uses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2000sulphuric_acid.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/2000sulphuric_acid.PNG/300px-2000sulphuric_acid.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/2000sulphuric_acid.PNG/450px-2000sulphuric_acid.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/2000sulphuric_acid.PNG/600px-2000sulphuric_acid.PNG 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2000sulphuric_acid.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sulfuric acid production in 2000</div></div></div>
<p>Sulfuric acid is a very important commodity chemical, and indeed, a nation's sulfuric acid production is a good indicator of its industrial strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> World production in 2004 was about 180 million <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">tonnes</a>, with the following geographic distribution: Asia 35%, North America (including Mexico) 24%, Africa 11%, Western Europe 10%, Eastern Europe and Russia 10%, Australia and Oceania 7%, South America 7%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Most of this amount (≈60%) is consumed for fertilizers, particularly superphosphates, ammonium phosphate and ammonium sulfates. About 20% is used in chemical industry for production of detergents, synthetic resins, dyestuffs, pharmaceuticals, petroleum catalysts, insecticides and <a href="/wiki/Antifreeze" title="Antifreeze">antifreeze</a>, as well as in various processes such as oil well acidicizing, aluminium reduction, paper sizing, water treatment. About 6% of uses are related to <a href="/wiki/Pigment" title="Pigment">pigments</a> and include paints, <a href="/wiki/Enamel_paint" title="Enamel paint">enamels</a>, printing inks, coated fabrics and paper, and the rest is dispersed into a multitude of applications such as production of explosives, <a href="/wiki/Cellophane" title="Cellophane">cellophane</a>, acetate and viscose textiles, lubricants, non-ferrous metals, and batteries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_production_of_chemicals">Industrial production of chemicals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sulfuric_acid&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Industrial production of chemicals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The major use for sulfuric acid is in the "wet method" for the production of <a href="/wiki/Phosphoric_acid" title="Phosphoric acid">phosphoric acid</a>, used for manufacture of <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphate</a> <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertilizers</a>. In this method, phosphate rock is used, and more than 100 million tonnes are processed annually. This raw material is shown below as <a href="/wiki/Fluorapatite" title="Fluorapatite">fluorapatite</a>, though the exact composition may vary. This is treated with 93% sulfuric acid to produce <a href="/wiki/Calcium_sulfate" title="Calcium sulfate">calcium sulfate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_fluoride" title="Hydrogen fluoride">hydrogen fluoride</a> (HF) and <a href="/wiki/Phosphoric_acid" title="Phosphoric acid">phosphoric acid</a>. The HF is removed as <a href="/wiki/Hydrofluoric_acid" title="Hydrofluoric acid">hydrofluoric acid</a>. The overall process can be represented as:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\ce {{\overset {fluorapatite}{Ca5F(PO4)3}}+{5H2SO4}+10H2O-&gt;{\overset {calcium~sulfate}{5CaSO4.2H2O}}+{HF}+3H3PO4}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
